Job Moves: who is hiring and where

By FT reporters 
2,136 words
19 July 2016
16:50
Financial Times (FT.Com)
FTCOM
English
Copyright 2016 The Financial Times Ltd. All rights reserved. Please do not cut and paste FT articles and redistribute by email or post to the web. 

The latest job moves in the trading industry and coverage of people making the news in the world s financial capitals

BNY Mellon names Kablawi to run European investment services unit

BNY Mellon has appointed Hani Kablawi to head a carved-out role that focuses on the European investment services business of the US custodian bank.

Mr Kablawi, who has been at BNY Mellon for nearly 20 years, will become head of investment services in Europe, the Middle East and Africa (Emea). The division generates most of BNY s revenues in the region and was previously shared with the regional chairman s role.

It will bring together under one unit BNY Mellon s services for investors and banks across asset servicing, alternative investments, corporate trust, broker-dealer, depositary receipts and treasury operations.

Mr Kablawi, who was formerly head of asset servicing in Emea, will report to Brian Shea, chief executive of investment services and Michael Cole-Fontayn , the regional division s chairman. Daron Pearce has been promoted to replace Mr Kablawi as chief executive of asset servicing for the region. (Philip Stafford, July 19)

ICE Futures Europe promotes Williams to COO role

ICE Futures Europe, the London-based derivatives exchange, has promoted Stuart Williams to become its new chief operating officer. He takes over a role that had been held by David Peniket, who is also the group s president. His appointment was effective from July 15, the exchange confirmed.

Mr Williams had previously been corporate development director at ICE Futures Europe and will report to Mr Peniket. Mr Williams, who joined ICE when the US exchange bought NYSE Euronext for $11bn in 2013, had been part of some of ICE  s biggest internal projects of recent years, such as moving clearing of derivatives contracts from LCH to ICE Clear Europe in 2013 and switching trading on Liffe to ICE in 2014. He has also been a management consultant for Protiviti and Accenture. (Philip Stafford, July 19)

LCH promotes Maguire to global rates role

LCH Group, the world s largest swaps clearing house, has promoted Daniel Maguire to an expanded role as global head of its rates and foreign exchange derivatives business.

Mr Maguire will be responsible for the development of listed and OTC rates and FX derivatives at LCH. He has been head of SwapClear, its over-the-counter (OTC) swaps and listed rates business for the last two years, and begins on May 1.

At the same time LCH also appointed Paddy Boyle, a former Goldman Sachs trader, as head of FX product. Mr Boyle was previously global head of G10 FX options at Goldman Sachs and was a member of the Bank of England joint standing committee on FX. He will report to Mr Maguire. (Philip Stafford, April 26)

Euronext s CFO Dauge to join fintech start-up

Amaury Dauge is to end his 15-year career at Euronext , the European exchanges operator, after announcing he will step down to join a financial technology company in New York.

He will be replaced by Giorgio Modica, a former banker at BNP Paribas, as Euronext  s new chief executive Stphane Boujnah reorganises the company s finance team.

Mr Dauge became chief financial officer in 2014 and oversaw Euronext  s demerger from former US parent Intercontinental Exchange , and its flotation on four bourses in Europe. He will leave on June 1st.

Mr Modica was previously a senior corporate financier focusing on the stock exchange sector globally, as well as for the Italian and Spanish markets. He advised NYSE Euronext during its ill-fated attempt to merge with Deutsche Brse , as well as the subsequent IPO once NYSE Euronext was acquired by ICE . He has also worked at HSBC in Milan and MCC/Capitalia in Rome.

The appointments come amid heightened speculation that Euronext may join in potential exchange consolidation and reshuffle of assets. Deutsche Brse is planning to merge with the London Stock Exchange Group but it may face a bid from ICE . The US group has already indicated it would be willing to sell the LSE  s Borsa Italiana , according to two people familiar with the talks.

At the same time Mr Boujnah also appointed Camille Beudin, a former mergers and acquisitions banker as Euronext  s new head of M&A. She previously worked at Deutsche Bank , RBS and ABN Amro .

 Giorgio has been so close to Euronext for so many years that he was the natural person to lead the finance team at Euronext ,  said Mr Boujnah. (Philip Stafford, April 19)

LSE names Ross as chief executive of CurveGlobal

The London Stock Exchange Group has filled the chief executive gap at CurveGlobal, its upcoming new interest rate derivatives joint venture, by naming Andrew Ross of Morgan Stanley to the position.

The position has been unfilled since the LSE said in October it would lead a 30m bank-backed futures trading venue that to compete in European markets dominated by Deutsche Brse and Intercontinental Exchange . Two years in preparation, CurveGlobal represents the biggest push by the LSE into interest rate futures since it was beaten to the 550m sale of Liffe, the London derivatives market, by Euronext in 2002.

At Morgan Stanley , Mr Ross was responsible for agency-listed derivative electronic trading and was also European head of clearing. In his 10-year career at the bank, Mr Ross also been head of CVA trading in London.

 CurveGlobal s success will be built on its ability to bring together a broad swath of exchange-traded derivatives and OTC market participants including the buy and sell sides, prop trading firms and market makers,  said Michael Davie , chairman of CurveGlobal.  It s therefore vital that our chief executive has the depth of experience and relationship with each of these communities, which is why I m delighted that Andrew will be taking on the role. 

The LSE added that France s BNP Paribas had become the seventh shareholder of CurveGlobal on January 29. Bank of America Merrill Lynch , Goldman Sachs , Barclays , Citi, JPMorgan and Socit Gnrale are also backing the project, as is the Chicago Board Options Exchange , the US exchange that owns the Vix volatility indices. The LSE will contribute 9.5m, and the banks and CBOE a further 20.5m. (Philip Stafford, February 5)

Intercontinental Exchange appoints Jackson as CCO

Intercontinental Exchange , the US exchanges operator, has reshuffled several senior executive positions following two recent major purchases.

The Atlanta-headquartered group on Tuesday said it had promoted Ben Jackson , president and chief operating officer of ICE Futures US, to the newly-created role of chief commercial officer. He will be responsible for integration planning and execution of ICE  s acquisitions and joint ventures.

Last month ICE bought Interactive Data , the OTC markets data business in December for $5.2bn, and Trayport , a European energy trading business, from BGC Partners for $650m in shares.

Lynn Martin , president and chief operating officer of ICE Data Services, has been given responsibility for Interactive Data , the OTC markets data business ICE acquired in December for $5.2bn. The unit she heads includes ICE derivatives and New York Stock Exchange market data, analytics and connectivity services.

Trabue Bland, ICE vice-president of regulation, will replace Mr Jackson as president of ICE Futures US. Mr Bland joined ICE in 2007 from the Commodity Futures Trading Commission where he was counsel to then CFTC chairman Walt Lukken .

The appointments are effective from February 1. All three will report to Jeff Sprecher , ICE group chief executive.  These promotions reflect our commitment to delivering on our strategic and financial objectives. And they reflect the contributions of these leaders in serving our customers in an evolving landscape, while establishing the next phase of our company s growth,  said Mr Sprecher. (Philip Stafford, January 26)

Wall retires from chief executive role at Marex Spectron

John Wall is to retire as chief executive of Marex Spectron after more than three years at the helm amid a wide-ranging board reshuffle at the UK commodities broker.

As part of the changes Jeremy Isaacs , the group s non-executive chairman and a key figure in the creation of the Marex business, will also step back from his role.

The duo have played a key role in short life of the company, whose modern incarnation was created when Marex bought by JRJ Group, a private equity firm founded by Mr Isaacs, former head of Lehman s European operations. In the intervening six years it has grown rapidly by hiring staff and purchasing smaller brokers, such as the 94.5m deal for Spectron, in 2011. Mr Wall, who had been at UBS for more than 25 years until his appointment at Marex, was appointed in part to integrate the Marex and Spectron companies.

Mr Wall will be replaced by Ian Lowitt, the group s chief financial officer, who will also move from New York to London to take over. Rob Watts, the group s financial controller, will become Marex s new CFO.

Both appointments take effect from Friday eighth January and remain subject to regulatory approval.

 With the firm in excellent shape, I feel that now is the right time for me to step back. It has been a privilege to lead this great company and I have no doubt that Ian is the right person to take charge of the next stage of its development,  said Mr Wall.

Mr Isaacs will be succeeded by Simon Heale , a non-executive director and former chief executive of the London Metal Exchange . Mr Isaacs will remain on the board. (Philip Stafford, January 6)

Euronext appoints former Tullet executive to lead FICC push

Euronext has appointed Paul Humphrey , a former executive at interdealer broker Tullett Prebon, to help the European exchanges operator develop a strategy to exploit rapidly-changing fixed income, rates and foreign exchange markets.

Mr Humphrey, who had been working at Thomson Reuters as a consultant, will join the group on January 4 with the title of head of fixed income, rates and FX (FICC) strategy. He was previously chief executive of Tullett s electronic broking and information business until the summer of 2014. He has also worked at ABN Amro , Van der Moolen, SLK/Goldman Sachs and ICAP.

His appointment comes as exchanges are increasingly eyeing markets that have long been dominated by banks, which continue to make billions of dollars in profits from it each year. Exchanges have generally been unable to establish a presence in fixed income and forex markets. However a combination of unlawful activity by banks, deep structural change and the emergence of cheap and reliable technology that has allowed alternative ways of trading to emerge. Euronext operates stock, commodity and derivatives markets around the region but has little OTC business.

Mr Humphrey will report to Lee Hodgkinson , head of markets and global sales, who said:  His appointment further strengthens our senior leadership team and his vast experience and strong vision will help us fulfil our growth ambitions in an important sector of the business.  (Philip Stafford, December 2)

Preuss to step away from Eurex role in Deutsche Brse reorganisation

Deutsche Brse , Europe s largest exchanges operator by market capitalisation, has unveiled a wide-ranging internal reorganisation that will see Andreas Preuss step away from his role as head of the Eurex derivatives exchange.

The internal reshaping comes five months after Carsten Kengeter , a former UBS banker, became chief executive with a plan to  put client focus at the heart of its structure.  In a statement on Wednesday, Deutsche Brse said it would create a new  Clients, Products and Core Markets  unit that will encompass its derivatives trading, clearing and settlement business. It will be headed by Jeffrey Tessler , chief executive of its Clearstream settlement business.

Mr Preuss, deputy chief executive and for many years Deutsche Brse  s most senior representative at industry events, will become chief executive of a new division, called  IT & Operations, Data & New Asset Classes . It will combine Deutsche Brse   market data unit, the European Energy Exchange and 360T, the foreign exchange trading network the company bought for  725m over the summer.

The group s cash equities business, which includes the well-known Frankfurt Stock Exchange Xetra, will be separated from the Eurex derivatives business and given its own divisional status  given its high political as well as macroeconomic importance , the company said. The enlarged division, named  Cash Market, Pre-IPO & Growth Financing , will include certificates and warrant businesses and the creation of an  innovative pre-IPO market . It will be led by Hauke Stars, who was previously responsible for Deutsche Brse  s market data division and the renewal of its IT infrastructure.

Mr Kengeter will be directly responsible for group strategy, mergers and acquisitions as well as government relations. (Philip Stafford, November 12)

Bloomberg Beta Launches Second $75 Million Fund

By Deborah Gage 
191 words
19 July 2016
22:13
The Wall Street Journal Online
WSJO
English
Copyright 2016 Dow Jones & Company, Inc. All Rights Reserved. 

Bloomberg Beta, the corporate venture capital arm of Bloomberg L.P., closed a second fund of $75 million, the same size as its first fund.

The firm says the fund's mission is to back startups that make businesses work better, building on the group's special interest in machine learning. Since it raised its first fund three years ago, three of its investments have been acquired, although the firm declined to say which ones.

Bloomberg Beta, with offices in New York and San Francisco, takes an unconventional approach to venture capital and has a minimal website. Instead, it publishes its internal operating manual publicly on GitHub, a repository for open source code.

The firm also takes a data-driven approach to investments, using a program called Future Founders, which tries to predict who is most likely to start companies.

Partners in Bloomberg Beta include Roy Bahat, Karin Klein, James Cham and Shivon Zilis.

Recent investments include Orbital Insight Inc., which applies data to understanding national and global trends, and AppZen Inc., which uses artificial intelligence to automate expense reports.

KKR, Warburg Pincus Might Hail Indonesia's Go-Jek

By Alec Macfarlane and Rick Carew in Hong Kong and P.R. Venkat in Singapore 
576 words
18 July 2016
The Wall Street Journal (Asia Edition)
AWSJ
B8
English
Copyright 2016 Dow Jones & Company, Inc. All Rights Reserved. 

Big-name investors KKR & Co. and Warburg Pincus LLC are taking the "Uber bet" to a new level as they consider an investment in an Indonesian motorcycle-hailing app that would value the startup at more than $1 billion.

The private-equity firms are in discussions to participate in a fundraising round for PT Go-Jek that could raise around $400 million and value the Indonesian company at about $1.2 billion, including the fresh funds, according to people familiar with the matter. Go-Jek, named after the motorcycle taxis, or ojeks, that customers can order through its app, is courting new and existing investors for the fundraising effort.

The people familiar with the situation said the round hasn't been completed and that the terms and participating investors could change.

Investors world-wide are pouring money into ride-hailing apps that are burning through cash to fund subsidies to attract drivers to their platforms. Go-Jek offers cheap, on-demand motorcycle taxis that can be booked through smartphones. The company offers fixed prices and pickups, meaning passengers don't need to haggle over prices at motorbike stands. It has also expanded its offerings into on-demand grocery shopping, delivery services, masseuses and beauticians, and has also ventured into offering cars and minivans.

If successful, Go-Jek's fundraising round would elevate it into the small club of Southeast Asian startups valued at more than $1 billion. Beyond its larger competitor GrabTaxi Holdings Pte Ltd., other billion-dollar startups include online game and messaging business Garena Interactive Holding Ltd. -- valued at about $3.75 billion in a March funding round -- and e-commerce company Lazada Group. In April, China's Alibaba Group Holding Ltd. agreed to pay $1 billion for a majority stake in Lazada.

Gridlock on the streets of Indonesia, Southeast Asia's most populous country and its largest economy, makes motorbike services popular for customers looking to cut through traffic.

Go-Jek competes for Indonesian passengers with ride-hailing companies such as U.S.-based Uber Technologies Inc., whose valuation of nearly $68 billion makes it the world's most valuable startup, and Singapore-based GrabTaxi, which operates across Southeast Asia and was valued at $1.6 billion in a funding round last year. Indonesia is home to more than 250 million people. About 30 million of them live in Jakarta, the capital.

Go-Jek launched its app in January 2015 and operates in 10 Indonesian cities. Both Uber and Grab began as car-hailing companies but have also moved into offering motorbikes. In 2014, Grab inaugurated GrabBike, which now operates in five cities in Indonesia. Uber also started offering motorcycle bookings in February with UberMotor, which it offers in three Indonesian cities. Go-Jek's app was the most-downloaded of the three companies in Indonesia in the first quarter of this year, according to mobile-app analytics firm App Annie, followed by Grab, and then Uber.

Go-Jek has been burning through cash as it provides subsidies to attract riders. The company spent $73 million between October 2015 and March 2016 to expand its business, leaving it with just over $100 million in the bank as of March, according to an investor presentation viewed by The Wall Street Journal.

COMPANIES
DCM Ventures raises $770m as VC funding hits 15-year high; Financial services

By Leslie Hook in San Francisco 
368 words
15 July 2016
Financial Times
FTFT
USA Ed1
15
English
Copyright 2016 The Financial Times Ltd. All rights reserved. Please do not cut and paste FT articles and redistribute by email or post to the web. 

Venture capital firm DCM Ventures has raised a fresh $770m from backers, including Asia's Tencent, Baidu and SoftBank, at a time when investors are pouring more money into VC funds, despite a cooling in Silicon Valley.

Investments in venture capital firms hit a 15-year high during the first half of this year, underscoring strong investor appetite even though the valuations of some prominent start-ups have been called into question .

Venture capital firms with ties to Asia have been particularly active, with two big rounds closed this week by firms that invest in tech start-ups in the region.

DCM Ventures, with more than $3bn under management, said yesterday that its new fund would split investments between the US and Asia, where previous investment targets have included Renren and Kakao Talk.

Tech investor Jim Breyer and IDG Capital also announced a $1bn fund earlier this week that will invest primarily in start-ups inside and outside China.

Mr Breyer acknowledged that the mood of the market had shifted. "We are in a global late-stage valuation market of increased uncertainty," he said, adding that late-stage start-ups with highly priced shares required more due diligence.

Investing outside Silicon Valley does not eliminate that challenge, he added. "The risk is about the same, in terms of late-stage valuation risk in Silicon Valley versus China."

However, he emphasised that areas such as machine learning and artificial intelligence still provided big opportunities for start-up growth.

The fundraising news from the two firms comes after venture capital firms raised $8.8bn in the second quarter of this year, according to a study by Thomson Reuters and the National Venture Capital Association .

Although second-quarter fundraising was below first-quarter levels, it brings the first half total to $22.9bn, the highest investment levels since the dotcom era.

David Chao , a partner at DCM Ventures, said that the backing of Asian tech companies in its latest round reflects its global ambitions. The emergence of Baidu, Tencent and Alibaba as tech powerhouses have boosted their investments in Silicon Valley.

Mobile advertising tech company Mobvista has purchased GameAnalytics, an analytic specialist for game developers. Financial terms of the deal weren't disclosed.

Copenhagen-based GameAnalytics has raised more than $8 million in funding from investors including Sunstone Capital, CrunchFund and Beta Angels. The company will continue to operate as an independent platform providing free analytics within Mobvista.

Mobile advertising platform Mobvista is backed by investors including Netease Capital, China Securities Co. Ltd. and Haitong Kaiyuan Investment Co. Ltd. Its clients include Baidu, Tencent, Alibaba, Uber, Electronic Arts, SGN and Machinezone.

Mobvista, based in Guangzhou, China, acquired NativeX, a Minnesota-based mobile ad monetization firm, for $25 million in February.

BlackRock: a rock in a hard place

307 words
14 July 2016
20:27
Financial Times (FT.Com)
FTCOM
English
Copyright 2016 The Financial Times Ltd. All rights reserved. Please do not cut and paste FT articles and redistribute by email or post to the web. 

Managing other people s money is no fun these days. More than four-fifths of US large-cap fund managers failed to beat the S&P 500 index s returns in the past five years, "http://us.spindices.com/search/?ContentType=SPIVA". Investors are wising up, buying cheaper index-tracking products or demanding lower fees. Morale and revenues are falling in tandem.

BlackRock, which runs active and passive funds, released earnings on Thursday. Assets under management are slightly up, and fees slightly down compared with last year s second quarter. Over a five-year period 51 per cent of actively managed fundamental equity strategies have beaten their benchmark and so have 92 per cent of their scientific strategies which rely on data, machine learning and modern technology.

Its iShares division, acquired from Barclays in 2009, accounts for about a quarter of BlackRock s $4.9tn of assets under management, and for 38 per cent of all "http://www.ft.com/cms/s/0/8d046d88-2020-11e6-aa98-db1e01fabc0c.html" assets globally.

The company s platform is well diversified across client types, asset classes and strategy types, so when investors switch allocations, they don t need to turn to a different provider: this year they pulled $20bn out of equities but allocated $58bn into BlackRock s fixed-income funds, reflecting the market s risk-off mood. BlackRock s technological prowess supports its ability to create new products, such as  smart beta  strategies, that enhance returns. Few asset managers can credibly combine bottom-up fundamental analysis with high-tech analytics.

Investors should expect no magic, however. BlackRock is well positioned among asset managers, but the pressures on the industry show no sign of relenting. Expect BlackRock s assets under management to keep growing, and the fees it charges for each dollar managed to keep falling.

Pro Private Markets
Bay Dynamics Grabs $23M

By Cat Zakrzewski 
134 words
13 July 2016
12:30
The Wall Street Journal Online
WSJO
English
Copyright 2016 Dow Jones & Company, Inc. All Rights Reserved. 

Bay Dynamics Inc . has raised $23 million to help companies gather cyberrisk analytics.

After high-profile hacks such as the 2013 Target Corp . breach, executives are paying closer attention to cybersecurity. But cybersecurity professionals have struggled to translate cyberthreats into business definitions of risk.

That is where Bay Dynamics ' Risk Fabric tool comes in. It takes information from an enterprise's security tools and reports information about those risks to business leaders, incident responders and security leaders.

"Companies need to move away from speaking in bits and bytes, to speaking in the language of risk," said Bay Dynamics Chief Executive Feris Rifai .

Carrick Capital Partners led the Series B funding. Comcast Ventures also participated.
